Unlike hardware (physical components), software is intangible - it\'s the code that makes hardware useful.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-explanation">\n                    <p><strong>Simple definition:</strong> Hardware = the physical machine. Software = the instructions that tell the machine what to do.</p>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n\n            <!-- Section 2 -->\n            <section class="lesson-section">\n                <h2>Types of Software</h2>\n                \n                <h3>System Software</h3>\n                <p>Software that manages computer hardware and provides a platform for running applications.</p>\n                <ul style="margin-left: 1.5rem; color: var(--text-gray);">\n                    <li><strong>Operating Systems:</strong> Windows, macOS, Linux</li>\n                    <li><strong>Device Drivers:</strong> Software that controls hardware devices</li>\n                    <li><strong>Utilities:</strong> Antivirus, disk cleanup, backup tools</li>\n                </ul>\n                \n                <h3>Application Software</h3>\n                <p>Programs designed for end-users to perform specific tasks.</p>\n                <ul style="margin-left: 1.5rem; color: var(--text-gray);">\n                    <li><strong>Productivity:</strong> Microsoft Word, Excel, Google Docs</li>\n                    <li><strong>Communication:</strong> Email clients, messaging apps</li>\n                    <li><strong>Entertainment:</strong> Games, media players</li>\n                    <li><strong>Creative:</strong> Photoshop, video editors</li>\n                </ul>\n                \n                <h3>Programming Software</h3>\n                <p>Tools used to create other software.</p>\n                <ul style="margin-left: 1.5rem; color: var(--text-gray);">\n                    <li><strong>IDEs:</strong> Integrated Development Environments (VS Code, PyCharm)</li>\n                    <li><strong>Compilers:</strong> Convert source code to machine code</li>\n                    <li><strong>Debuggers:</strong> Help find and fix errors in code</li>\n                </ul>\n            </section>\n\n            <!-- Section 3 -->\n            <section class="lesson-section">\n                <h2>How Programs are Created</h2>\n                <p>Software development involves writing code in programming languages that humans can understand, then converting it to a form computers can execute.</p>\n                \n                <h3>The Programming Process</h3>\n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code><span class="comment">// Software Development Process:</span>\n\n<span class="number">1.</span> <span class="function">Write Source Code</span>\n    ↓   <span class="comment">// Human-readable instructions</span>\n    \n<span class="number">2.</span> <span class="function">Compile/Interpret</span>\n    ↓   <span class="comment">// Convert to machine-readable format</span>\n    \n<span class="number">3.</span> <span class="function">Execute</span>\n    ↓   <span class="comment">// Computer runs the instructions</span>\n    \n<span class="number">4.</span> <span class="function">Output</span>\n        <span class="comment">// Results shown to user</span></code></pre>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n\n            <!-- Section 4 -->\n            <section class="lesson-section">\n                <h2>Source Code vs Machine Code</h2>\n                \n                <h3>Source Code</h3>\n                <p>Instructions written by programmers in a programming language like Python, JavaScript, or C++. It\'s human-readable but computers can\'t understand it directly.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code><span class="comment">// Example source code in Python:</span>\n<span class="keyword">def</span> <span class="function">greet</span>(<span class="variable">name</span>):\n    <span class="keyword">return</span> <span class="string">f"Hello, {name}!"</span>\n\n<span class="variable">message</span> = <span class="function">greet</span>(<span class="string">"World"</span>)\n<span class="keyword">print</span>(<span class="variable">message</span>)</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <h3>Machine Code</h3>\n                <p>The binary instructions that the CPU actually executes. Each CPU architecture has its own machine code format.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code><span class="comment">// Same program in machine code (simplified):</span>\n<span class="number">10110000</span> <span class="number">01100001</span>\n<span class="number">10111000</span> <span class="number">00000100</span>\n<span class="number">11000110</span> <span class="number">00000111</span>\n<span class="number">01010110</span> <span class="number">10111000</span>\n<span class="comment">// ... many more lines of binary</span></code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <div class="tip-box">\n                    <svg viewBox="0 0 24 24" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg">\n                        <path d="M12 2C6.48 2 2 6.48 2 12s4.48 10 10 10 10-4.48 10-10S17.52 2 12 2zm1 15h-2v-6h2v6zm0-8h-2V7h2v2z"/>\n                    </svg>\n                    <p><strong>Imagine:</strong> If programmers had to write machine code directly, even simple programs would take months and be nearly impossible to debug!</p>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n\n            <!-- Section 5 -->\n            <section class="lesson-section">\n                <h2>Compilers vs Interpreters</h2>\n                <p>There are two main ways to convert source code to machine code:</p>\n                \n                <h3>Compiled Languages</h3>\n                <p>A compiler translates the entire program into machine code before execution. The result is a standalone executable file.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code><span class="comment">// Compiled Language Workflow:</span>\n<span class="variable">Source Code</span> → [<span class="function">Compiler</span>] → <span class="variable">Executable</span> → [<span class="function">Run</span>]\n\n<span class="comment">// Examples: C, C++, Rust, Go</span>\n<span class="comment">// Pros: Fast execution, optimized code</span>\n<span class="comment">// Cons: Must recompile after changes, platform-specific</span></code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <h3>Interpreted Languages</h3>\n                <p>An interpreter reads and executes code line by line, translating on the fly.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code><span class="comment">// Interpreted Language Workflow:</span>\n<span class="variable">Source Code</span> → [<span class="function">Interpreter</span>] → <span class="variable">Direct Execution</span>\n\n<span class="comment">// Examples: Python, JavaScript, Ruby</span>\n<span class="comment">// Pros: Easier to test, platform-independent</span>\n<span class="comment">// Cons: Slower execution, needs interpreter installed</span></code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <h3>Hybrid Approach (JIT)</h3>\n                <p>Modern languages often use Just-In-Time compilation, combining benefits of both approaches. The code is interpreted initially but frequently-used parts are compiled for speed.</p>\n                <ul style="margin-left: 1.5rem; color: var(--text-gray);">\n                    <li>JavaScript in modern browsers</li>\n                    <li>Java (compiles to bytecode, then JIT)</li>\n                    <li>Python with PyPy</li>\n                </ul>\n            </section>\n\n            <!-- Section 6 -->\n            <section class="lesson-section">\n                <h2>How Programs Use Memory</h2>\n                <p>When a program runs, it uses different types of memory:</p>\n                \n                <h3>Stack Memory</h3>\n                <p>Fast, organized memory for function calls and local variables. Automatically managed - variables are "popped off" when functions end.</p>\n                \n                <h3>Heap Memory</h3>\n                <p>Larger, flexible memory for dynamic data. Must be managed (manually in some languages, automatically with garbage collection in others).</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code><span class="comment">// Memory usage example (Python):</span>\n\n<span class="keyword">def</span> <span class="function">calculate</span>():\n    <span class="variable">x</span> = <span class="number">10</span>        <span class="comment">// Stored on stack</span>\n    <span class="variable">y</span> = <span class="number">20</span>        <span class="comment">// Stored on stack</span>\n    <span class="keyword">return</span> <span class="variable">x</span> + <span class="variable">y</span>\n\n<span class="comment">// When function ends, x and y are removed from stack</span>\n\n<span class="variable">data</span> = [<span class="number">1</span>, <span class="number">2</span>, <span class="number">3</span>, <span class="number">4</span>, <span class="number">5</span>]  <span class="comment">// List stored on heap</span>\n<span class="comment">// List persists until no longer needed, then garbage collected</span></code></pre>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n\n            <!-- Section 7 -->\n            <section class="lesson-section">\n                <h2>APIs and Libraries</h2>\n                <p>Programmers don\'t write everything from scratch. They use pre-built code:</p>\n                \n                <h3>Libraries</h3>\n                <p>Collections of pre-written code that you can use in your programs. They provide common functionality so you don\'t have to reinvent the wheel.</p>\n                \n                <h3>APIs (Application Programming Interfaces)</h3>\n                <p>Defined ways for software components to communicate. APIs let you use functionality from other programs or services.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code><span class="comment">// Example: Using a library in Python</span>\n<span class="keyword">import</span> <span class="variable">random</span>  <span class="comment">// Import the random library</span>\n\n<span class="comment">// Use a function from the library</span>\n<span class="variable">number</span> = <span class="variable">random</span>.<span class="function">randint</span>(<span class="number">1</span>, <span class="number">100</span>)\n<span class="keyword">print</span>(<span class="variable">number</span>)  <span class="comment">// Prints random number 1-100</span>\n\n<span class="comment">// Without the library, you\'d have to write</span>\n<span class="comment">// all the random number generation code yourself!</span></code></pre>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n\n            <!-- Key Takeaways -->\n            <section class="lesson-section">\n                <h2>Key Takeaways</h2>\n                <div class="tip-box">\n                    <svg viewBox="0 0 24 24" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg">\n                        <path d="M12 2C6.48 2 2 6.48 2 12s4.48 10 10 10 10-4.48 10-10S17.52 2 12 2zm1 15h-2v-6h2v6zm0-8h-2V7h2v2z"/>\n                    </svg>\n                    <div>\n                        <p><strong>Remember:</strong></p>\n                        <ul style="margin-top: 0.5rem; margin-left: 1.5rem;">\n                            <li><strong>Software:</strong> Instructions that tell hardware what to do</li>\n                            <li><strong>Source Code:</strong> Human-readable programming instructions</li>\n                            <li><strong>Machine Code:</strong> Binary instructions CPUs understand</li>\n                            <li><strong>Compilers:</strong> Convert entire programs before execution</li>\n                            <li><strong>Interpreters:</strong> Execute code line by line</li>\n                            <li><strong>Libraries/APIs:</strong> Pre-built code you can reuse</li>\n                        </ul>\n                    </div>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n\n            <!-- Navigation -->\n            <div class="nav-buttons">\n                <a href="lesson4.html" class="nav-btn prev">← Previous: Operating Systems</a>\n                <a href="lesson6.html" class="nav-btn next">Next: Computer Networks →</a>\n            </div>\n        </div>\n    </main>\n\n    <!-- Footer -->\n    <footer class="footer">\n        <p>© 2024 Learner. Networks range from small home networks to the global Internet.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-explanation">\n                    <p><strong>Why Networks Matter:</strong> Without networks, each computer would be isolated. Networks enable email, web browsing, video calls, online gaming, and virtually everything we do with computers today.</p>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n\n            <!-- Section 2 -->\n            <section class="lesson-section">\n                <h2>Types of Networks</h2>\n                \n                <h3>PAN (Personal Area Network)</h3>\n                <p>Very short-range network around a person. Example: Bluetooth connections between your phone and headphones.</p>\n                \n                <h3>LAN (Local Area Network)</h3>\n                <p>Network in a limited area like a home, office, or building. Your home WiFi network is a LAN.</p>\n                \n                <h3>WAN (Wide Area Network)</h3>\n                <p>Network spanning large geographic areas. The Internet is the largest WAN.</p>\n                \n                <h3>WLAN (Wireless LAN)</h3>\n                <p>A LAN that uses wireless communication (WiFi) instead of cables.</p>\n                \n                <div class="tip-box">\n                    <svg viewBox="0 0 24 24" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg">\n                        <path d="M12 2C6.48 2 2 6.48 2 12s4.48 10 10 10 10-4.48 10-10S17.52 2 12 2zm1 15h-2v-6h2v6zm0-8h-2V7h2v2z"/>\n                    </svg>\n                    <p><strong>Key Point:</strong> The Internet is a network of networks. Your home network connects to your ISP\'s network, which connects to other networks worldwide.</p>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n\n            <!-- Section 3 -->\n            <section class="lesson-section">\n                <h2>Network Hardware</h2>\n                \n                <h3>Router</h3>\n                <p>Directs data between networks. Your home router connects your LAN to the Internet (WAN) and decides where to send data.</p>\n                \n                <h3>Switch</h3>\n                <p>Connects devices within a LAN. Unlike a router, it only handles local traffic between connected devices.</p>\n                \n                <h3>Modem</h3>\n                <p>Converts signals between your ISP\'s network and your home network. Often combined with routers in "gateway" devices.</p>\n                \n                <h3>Network Interface Card (NIC)</h3>\n                <p>Hardware that lets a computer connect to a network. Most computers have built-in WiFi and Ethernet NICs.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code><span class="comment">// Simplified network structure:</span>\n\n<span class="variable">Internet</span>\n    ↓\n<span class="function">Modem</span> (converts ISP signals)\n    ↓\n<span class="function">Router</span> (directs traffic, provides WiFi)\n    ↓\n<span class="function">Switch</span> (optional, expands wired connections)\n    ↓\n<span class="variable">Devices</span> (computers, phones, tablets)</code></pre>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n\n            <!-- Section 4 -->\n            <section class="lesson-section">\n                <h2>IP Addresses</h2>\n                <p>Every device on a network needs a unique address - like a postal address for your computer. This is called an IP (Internet Protocol) address.</p>\n                \n                <h3>IPv4 Addresses</h3>\n                <p>The traditional format: four numbers separated by dots. Each number ranges from 0-255.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code><span class="comment">// IPv4 Address Example:</span>\n<span class="number">192.168.1.1</span>\n\n<span class="comment">// Breakdown:</span>\n<span class="number">192</span>.<span class="number">168</span>.<span class="number">1</span>.<span class="number">1</span>\n ↑    ↑   ↑   ↑\n<span class="variable">0-255</span> for each section\n\n<span class="comment">// Total possible IPv4 addresses:</span>\n<span class="number">256</span> × <span class="number">256</span> × <span class="number">256</span> × <span class="number">256</span> ≈ <span class="number">4.3 billion</span></code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <h3>IPv6 Addresses</h3>\n                <p>With 4.3 billion IPv4 addresses running out, IPv6 was created with a much larger address space.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code><span class="comment">// IPv6 Address Example:</span>\n<span class="number">2001:0db8:85a3:0000:0000:8a2e:0370:7334</span>\n\n<span class="comment">// Uses hexadecimal (0-9, a-f)</span>\n<span class="comment">// 128 bits vs IPv4\'s 32 bits</span>\n<span class="comment">// Approximately 340 undecillion addresses!</span></code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <h3>Public vs Private IPs</h3>\n                <ul style="margin-left: 1.5rem; color: var(--text-gray);">\n                    <li><strong>Public IP:</strong> Unique address visible on the Internet. Assigned by your ISP.</li>\n                    <li><strong>Private IP:</strong> Used within local networks. Not directly accessible from the Internet.</li>\n                </ul>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code><span class="comment">// Common private IP ranges:</span>\n<span class="number">192.168.0.0</span> - <span class="number">192.168.255.255</span>  <span class="comment">// Home routers</span>\n<span class="number">10.0.0.0</span> - <span class="number">10.255.255.255</span>    <span class="comment">// Large organizations</span>\n<span class="number">172.16.0.0</span> - <span class="number">172.31.255.255</span>  <span class="comment">// Medium networks</span></code></pre>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n\n            <!-- Section 5 -->\n            <section class="lesson-section">\n                <h2>Ports and Protocols</h2>\n                \n                <h3>What are Ports?</h3>\n                <p>Ports are numbered channels that help route data to the right application on a device. Think of an IP address as a building address and ports as apartment numbers.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code><span class="comment">// Common port numbers:</span>\n<span class="number">80</span>   → <span class="variable">HTTP</span>   (web browsing)\n<span class="number">443</span>  → <span class="variable">HTTPS</span>  (secure web browsing)\n<span class="number">22</span>   → <span class="variable">SSH</span>    (secure remote access)\n<span class="number">25</span>   → <span class="variable">SMTP</span>   (email sending)\n<span class="number">53</span>   → <span class="variable">DNS</span>    (domain name system)\n<span class="number">3306</span> → <span class="variable">MySQL</span>  (database)\n\n<span class="comment">// Example: https://example.com:443</span>\n<span class="comment">// The :443 specifies the port (usually hidden for standard ports)</span></code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <h3>Common Protocols</h3>\n                <p>Protocols are standardized rules for communication:</p>\n                \n                <ul style="margin-left: 1.5rem; color: var(--text-gray);">\n                    <li><strong>HTTP/HTTPS:</strong> Transfers web pages</li>\n                    <li><strong>FTP:</strong> File transfers</li>\n                    <li><strong>SMTP/POP/IMAP:</strong> Email</li>\n                    <li><strong>DNS:</strong> Translates domain names to IP addresses</li>\n                    <li><strong>TCP:</strong> Reliable, connection-based data transfer</li>\n                    <li><strong>UDP:</strong> Fast, connectionless data transfer (used for streaming)</li>\n                </ul>\n                \n                <div class="code-explanation">\n                    <p><strong>TCP vs UDP:</strong> TCP guarantees data arrives correctly (like certified mail). UDP is faster but doesn\'t guarantee delivery (like regular mail). Video streaming uses UDP because speed matters more than perfection.</p>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n\n            <!-- Section 6 -->\n            <section class="lesson-section">\n                <h2>DNS (Domain Name System)</h2>\n                <p>DNS translates human-readable domain names to IP addresses. It\'s like the phonebook of the Internet.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code><span class="comment">// DNS Translation Example:</span>\n\n<span class="variable">You type:</span> www.google.com\n        ↓\n<span class="function">DNS Lookup</span> (finds the IP address)\n        ↓\n<span class="variable">Browser connects to:</span> <span class="number">142.250.190.46</span>\n\n<span class="comment">// Without DNS, you\'d have to memorize</span>\n<span class="comment">// IP addresses for every website!</span></code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <h3>How DNS Works</h3>\n                <ol style="margin-left: 1.5rem; color: var(--text-gray);">\n                    <li>You type a domain name in your browser</li>\n                    <li>Your computer checks its local cache</li>\n                    <li>If not found, it asks your ISP\'s DNS server</li>\n                    <li>If still not found, it asks root DNS servers</li>\n                    <li>The chain continues until the IP is found</li>\n                    <li>The result is cached for future use</li>\n                </ol>\n            </section>\n\n            <!-- Key Takeaways -->\n            <section class="lesson-section">\n                <h2>Key Takeaways</h2>\n                <div class="tip-box">\n                    <svg viewBox="0 0 24 24" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg">\n                        <path d="M12 2C6.48 2 2 6.48 2 12s4.48 10 10 10 10-4.48 10-10S17.52 2 12 2zm1 15h-2v-6h2v6zm0-8h-2V7h2v2z"/>\n                    </svg>\n                    <div>\n                        <p><strong>Remember:</strong></p>\n                        <ul style="margin-top: 0.5rem; margin-left: 1.5rem;">\n                            <li><strong>Network:</strong> Connected computers sharing resources</li>\n                            <li><strong>LAN:</strong> Local network; WAN: Wide-area network</li>\n                            <li><strong>Router:</strong> Directs traffic between networks</li>\n                            <li><strong>IP Address:</strong> Unique identifier for each device</li>\n                            <li><strong>Ports:</strong> Channels for routing data to applications</li>\n                            <li><strong>DNS:</strong> Translates domain names to IP addresses</li>\n                        </ul>\n                    </div>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n\n            <!-- Navigation -->\n            <div class="nav-buttons">\n                <a href="lesson5.html" class="nav-btn prev">← Previous: How Software Works</a>\n                <a href="lesson7.html" class="nav-btn next">Next: The Internet and Web →</a>\n            </div>\n        </div>\n    </main>\n\n    <!-- Footer -->\n    <footer class="footer">\n        <p>© 2024 Learner. Think of it as the road system.</p>\n                \n                <h3>The World Wide Web (WWW)</h3>\n                <p>The Web is a service that runs ON the Internet - a collection of websites and web pages linked together. Think of it as the vehicles and destinations on the roads.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-explanation">\n                    <p><strong>Simple comparison:</strong> The Internet is like the telephone network infrastructure. The Web is like one of the services that uses it (like calling a friend). Email, video streaming, and online gaming also use the Internet but aren\'t part of the Web.</p>\n                </div>\n                \n                <div class="tip-box">\n                    <svg viewBox="0 0 24 24" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg">\n                        <path d="M12 2C6.48 2 2 6.48 2 12s4.48 10 10 10 10-4.48 10-10S17.52 2 12 2zm1 15h-2v-6h2v6zm0-8h-2V7h2v2z"/>\n                    </svg>\n                    <p><strong>Key distinction:</strong> The Internet was created in the 1960s-70s. The World Wide Web was invented in 1989 by Tim Berners-Lee.</p>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n\n            <!-- Section 2 -->\n            <section class="lesson-section">\n                <h2>How the Web Works</h2>\n                <p>When you visit a website, a complex process happens in seconds:</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code><span class="comment">// The Web Request Process:</span>\n\n<span class="number">1.</span> <span class="variable">You type:</span> https://www.example.com\n    ↓\n<span class="number">2.</span> <span class="function">DNS Lookup:</span> Find the server\'s IP address\n    ↓\n<span class="number">3.</span> <span class="function">HTTP Request:</span> Browser sends request to server\n    ↓\n<span class="number">4.</span> <span class="function">Server Processing:</span> Server finds the webpage\n    ↓\n<span class="number">5.</span> <span class="function">HTTP Response:</span> Server sends files back\n    ↓\n<span class="number">6.</span> <span class="function">Rendering:</span> Browser displays the webpage</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <h3>Client-Server Model</h3>\n                <p>The web operates on a client-server model:</p>\n                <ul style="margin-left: 1.5rem; color: var(--text-gray);">\n                    <li><strong>Client:</strong> Your web browser (Chrome, Firefox, Safari) - it requests and displays content</li>\n                    <li><strong>Server:</strong> A computer that stores websites and sends them to clients when requested</li>\n                </ul>\n            </section>\n\n            <!-- Section 3 -->\n            <section class="lesson-section">\n                <h2>Web Technologies</h2>\n                \n                <h3>HTML (HyperText Markup Language)</h3>\n                <p>The structure of web pages. HTML defines what content appears on a page - headings, paragraphs, images, links.</p>\n                \n                <h3>CSS (Cascading Style Sheets)</h3>\n                <p>The styling of web pages. CSS controls how content looks - colors, fonts, layouts, animations.</p>\n                \n                <h3>JavaScript</h3>\n                <p>The behavior of web pages. JavaScript makes pages interactive - responding to clicks, loading new content, validating forms.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code><span class="comment">// How these technologies work together:</span>\n\n<span class="variable">HTML</span> → <span class="string">"What\'s on the page"</span>  <span class="comment">// Structure</span>\n<span class="variable">CSS</span>  → <span class="string">"How it looks"</span>      <span class="comment">// Presentation</span>\n<span class="variable">JS</span>   → <span class="string">"How it behaves"</span>    <span class="comment">// Behavior</span>\n\n<span class="comment">// Analogy:</span>\n<span class="comment">// HTML = skeleton (structure)</span>\n<span class="comment">// CSS = skin and clothes (appearance)</span>\n<span class="comment">// JavaScript = muscles and movement (behavior)</span></code></pre>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n\n            <!-- Section 4 -->\n            <section class="lesson-section">\n                <h2>URLs Explained</h2>\n                <p>A URL (Uniform Resource Locator) is the address of a web resource. Let\'s break one down:</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code><span class="comment">// URL Structure:</span>\n<span class="keyword">https</span>://<span class="variable">www</span>.<span class="function">example</span>.<span class="variable">com</span>/<span class="string">page</span>?<span class="variable">id</span>=<span class="number">123</span>#<span class="variable">section</span>\n\n<span class="comment">// Breakdown:</span>\n┌──────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐\n│ <span class="keyword">https</span>      → <span class="function">Protocol</span> (how to communicate)       │\n│ <span class="variable">www</span>        → <span class="function">Subdomain</span> (specific server)           │\n│ <span class="function">example</span>    → <span class="function">Domain name</span> (website identity)       │\n│ <span class="variable">com</span>        → <span class="function">Top-level domain</span> (TLD)              │\n│ <span class="string">/page</span>     → <span class="function">Path</span> (specific page)                   │\n│ <span class="variable">?id=123</span>   → <span class="function">Query parameters</span> (data sent to server)│\n│ <span class="variable">#section</span>  → <span class="function">Fragment</span> (jump to section on page)    │\n└──────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <h3>Common TLDs</h3>\n                <ul style="margin-left: 1.5rem; color: var(--text-gray);">\n                    <li><strong>.com:</strong> Commercial (most common)</li>\n                    <li><strong>.org:</strong> Organizations</li>\n                    <li><strong>.edu:</strong> Educational institutions</li>\n                    <li><strong>.gov:</strong> Government</li>\n                    <li><strong>.io:</strong> Tech startups (originally British Indian Ocean Territory)</li>\n                    <li><strong>.country codes:</strong> .uk, .ca, .de, .jp, etc.</li>\n                </ul>\n            </section>\n\n            <!-- Section 5 -->\n            <section class="lesson-section">\n                <h2>HTTP and HTTPS</h2>\n                \n                <h3>HTTP (HyperText Transfer Protocol)</h3>\n                <p>The rules for transferring web pages. It defines how clients and servers communicate.</p>\n                \n                <h3>HTTPS (HTTP Secure)</h3>\n                <p>Encrypted HTTP. It protects your data from being intercepted. Always look for the padlock icon in your browser!</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code><span class="comment">// HTTP Methods (types of requests):</span>\n\n<span class="keyword">GET</span>     → <span class="string">"Give me this page"</span>\n<span class="keyword">POST</span>    → <span class="string">"Here\'s data to process"</span>\n<span class="keyword">PUT</span>     → <span class="string">"Update this resource"</span>\n<span class="keyword">DELETE</span>  → <span class="string">"Remove this resource"</span>\n\n<span class="comment">// HTTP Status Codes:</span>\n<span class="number">200</span> → <span class="string">OK</span> (success)\n<span class="number">301</span> → <span class="string">Moved Permanently</span> (redirect)\n<span class="number">404</span> → <span class="string">Not Found</span> (page doesn\'t exist)\n<span class="number">500</span> → <span class="string">Internal Server Error</span> (server problem)</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <div class="tip-box">\n                    <svg viewBox="0 0 24 24" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg">\n                        <path d="M12 2C6.48 2 2 6.48 2 12s4.48 10 10 10 10-4.48 10-10S17.52 2 12 2zm1 15h-2v-6h2v6zm0-8h-2V7h2v2z"/>\n                    </svg>\n                    <p><strong>Security Tip:</strong> Never enter passwords or credit card info on non-HTTPS sites. Look for the padlock icon and "https://" in the URL.</p>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n\n            <!-- Section 6 -->\n            <section class="lesson-section">\n                <h2>Web Browsers</h2>\n                <p>Browsers are software that fetch, interpret, and display web pages. Popular browsers include:</p>\n                \n                <ul style="margin-left: 1.5rem; color: var(--text-gray);">\n                    <li><strong>Google Chrome:</strong> Most popular, fast, great developer tools</li>\n                    <li><strong>Mozilla Firefox:</strong> Privacy-focused, open source</li>\n                    <li><strong>Safari:</strong> Apple\'s browser, optimized for macOS and iOS</li>\n                    <li><strong>Microsoft Edge:</strong> Built on Chromium, integrated with Windows</li>\n                </ul>\n                \n                <h3>What Browsers Do</h3>\n                <ol style="margin-left: 1.5rem; color: var(--text-gray);">\n                    <li>Parse HTML to build the page structure</li>\n                    <li>Apply CSS to style elements</li>\n                    <li>Execute JavaScript for interactivity</li>\n                    <li>Handle user interactions (clicks, forms)</li>\n                    <li>Cache resources for faster loading</li>\n                </ol>\n            </section>\n\n            <!-- Section 7 -->\n            <section class="lesson-section">\n                <h2>Frontend vs Backend</h2>\n                \n                <h3>Frontend (Client-side)</h3>\n                <p>Everything the user sees and interacts with in the browser. Built with HTML, CSS, and JavaScript.</p>\n                \n                <h3>Backend (Server-side)</h3>\n                <p>The server-side logic that powers applications. Handles databases, authentication, and business logic. Built with languages like Python, Node.js, PHP, Ruby, or Java.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code><span class="comment">// Web Application Architecture:</span>\n\n┌─────────────────────────────────────────┐\n│              <span class="function">FRONTEND</span>                  │\n│  HTML + CSS + JavaScript (in browser)   │\n└─────────────────┬───────────────────────┘\n                  │ <span class="variable">HTTP requests</span>\n                  ↓\n┌─────────────────────────────────────────┐\n│              <span class="function">BACKEND</span>                   │\n│  Server (Python/Node.js/etc)            │\n│  ↓                                      │\n│  Database (MySQL/MongoDB/etc)           │\n└─────────────────────────────────────────┘</code></pre>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n\n            <!-- Key Takeaways -->\n            <section class="lesson-section">\n                <h2>Key Takeaways</h2>\n                <div class="tip-box">\n                    <svg viewBox="0 0 24 24" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg">\n                        <path d="M12 2C6.48 2 2 6.48 2 12s4.48 10 10 10 10-4.48 10-10S17.52 2 12 2zm1 15h-2v-6h2v6zm0-8h-2V7h2v2z"/>\n                    </svg>\n                    <div>\n                        <p><strong>Remember:</strong></p>\n                        <ul style="margin-top: 0.5rem; margin-left: 1.5rem;">\n                            <li><strong>Internet:</strong> Global network infrastructure</li>\n                            <li><strong>Web:</strong> Service running on the Internet</li>\n                            <li><strong>HTML/CSS/JS:</strong> The three core web technologies</li>\n                            <li><strong>URL:</strong> Address that identifies web resources</li>\n                            <li><strong>HTTPS:</strong> Secure, encrypted web communication</li>\n                            <li><strong>Frontend:</strong> User-facing; Backend: Server-side</li>\n                        </ul>\n                    </div>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n\n            <!-- Navigation -->\n            <div class="nav-buttons">\n                <a href="lesson6.html" class="nav-btn prev">← Previous: Computer Networks</a>\n                <a href="lesson8.html" class="nav-btn next">Next: Security Basics →</a>\n            </div>\n        </div>\n    </main>\n\n    <!-- Footer -->\n    <footer class="footer">\n        <p>© 2024 Learner. Every day, cybercriminals attempt to steal data, money, and identities. Understanding security basics helps protect yourself and others.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-explanation">\n                    <p><strong>The reality:</strong> There are malicious actors constantly scanning the Internet for vulnerable systems. A new computer connected to the Internet can be attacked within minutes.</p>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n\n            <!-- Section 2 -->\n            <section class="lesson-section">\n                <h2>Common Threats</h2>\n                \n                <h3>Malware (Malicious Software)</h3>\n                <p>Software designed to harm or exploit systems. Types include:</p>\n                <ul style="margin-left: 1.5rem; color: var(--text-gray);">\n                    <li><strong>Virus:</strong> Attaches to files, spreads when files are shared</li>\n                    <li><strong>Worm:</strong> Self-replicates across networks</li>\n                    <li><strong>Trojan:</strong> Disguises as legitimate software</li>\n                    <li><strong>Ransomware:</strong> Encrypts your files, demands payment</li>\n                    <li><strong>Spyware:</strong> Secretly monitors your activity</li>\n                </ul>\n                \n                <h3>Phishing</h3>\n                <p>Fake emails or websites that trick you into revealing passwords or personal information. They often impersonate banks, social media, or trusted companies.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code><span class="comment">// Example phishing email signs:</span>\n\n<span class="variable">From:</span> "Bank Security" &lt;security@bank-secure.xyz&gt;\n<span class="comment">// Suspicious domain (not your real bank)</span>\n\n<span class="variable">Subject:</span> URGENT: Your account will be closed!\n<span class="comment">// Creates panic to bypass critical thinking</span>\n\n<span class="variable">Link:</span> http://bank-verify.com/login\n<span class="comment">// Not the real bank website!</span>\n\n<span class="variable">Request:</span> "Click here to verify your password"\n<span class="comment">// Banks never ask for passwords via email</span></code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <h3>Social Engineering</h3>\n                <p>Manipulating people into revealing information or performing actions. The human element is often the weakest link in security.</p>\n                \n                <h3>Man-in-the-Middle Attacks</h3>\n                <p>An attacker intercepts communication between two parties, potentially reading or modifying the data.</p>\n            </section>\n\n            <!-- Section 3 -->\n            <section class="lesson-section">\n                <h2>Password Security</h2>\n                <p>Passwords are your first line of defense. Strong password practices are crucial:</p>\n                \n                <h3>Creating Strong Passwords</h3>\n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code><span class="comment">// Password Strength Examples:</span>\n\n<span class="keyword">WEAK</span>    → <span class="string">"password123"</span>      <span class="comment">// Common, easily guessed</span>\n<span class="keyword">WEAK</span>    → <span class="string">"john1990"</span>          <span class="comment">// Personal info</span>\n<span class="keyword">MEDIUM</span>  → <span class="string">"P@ssw0rd!"</span>         <span class="comment">// Common with substitutions</span>\n<span class="keyword">STRONG</span>  → <span class="string">"Xk9#mP2$vL5@nQ8!"</span>  <span class="comment">// Random, complex</span>\n<span class="keyword">STRONG</span>  → <span class="string">"correct-horse-battery-staple"</span> <span class="comment">// Long passphrase</span></code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <div class="tip-box">\n                    <svg viewBox="0 0 24 24" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg">\n                        <path d="M12 2C6.48 2 2 6.48 2 12s4.48 10 10 10 10-4.48 10-10S17.52 2 12 2zm1 15h-2v-6h2v6zm0-8h-2V7h2v2z"/>\n                    </svg>\n                    <p><strong>Best Practice:</strong> Use a password manager! It generates and stores unique, complex passwords for each account. You only need to remember one master password.</p>\n                </div>\n                \n                <h3>Two-Factor Authentication (2FA)</h3>\n                <p>Requires something you know (password) AND something you have (phone, security key). Even if someone steals your password, they can\'t access your account without the second factor.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code><span class="comment">// 2FA Types:</span>\n\n<span class="variable">SMS Code</span>     → Texted to your phone\n<span class="variable">Auth App</span>     → Google/Microsoft Authenticator\n<span class="variable">Hardware Key</span> → Physical device (YubiKey)\n<span class="variable">Biometric</span>    → Fingerprint, face recognition</code></pre>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n\n            <!-- Section 4 -->\n            <section class="lesson-section">\n                <h2>Encryption</h2>\n                <p>Encryption converts data into a coded form that can only be read with the correct key. It protects your data both in transit and at rest.</p>\n                \n                <h3>How Encryption Works</h3>\n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code><span class="comment">// Simplified Encryption:</span>\n\n<span class="variable">Original</span>: "Hello World"\n    ↓\n<span class="function">Encryption</span> (using key)\n    ↓\n<span class="variable">Encrypted</span>: "U2FsdGVkX1+abc123..."\n    ↓\n<span class="function">Decryption</span> (using same key)\n    ↓\n<span class="variable">Original</span>: "Hello World"</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <h3>Encryption Types</h3>\n                <ul style="margin-left: 1.5rem; color: var(--text-gray);">\n                    <li><strong>Symmetric:</strong> Same key encrypts and decrypts (faster, but key must be shared securely)</li>\n                    <li><strong>Asymmetric:</strong> Two keys - public (encrypt) and private (decrypt). Used in HTTPS.</li>\n                </ul>\n                \n                <h3>Where You See Encryption</h3>\n                <ul style="margin-left: 1.5rem; color: var(--text-gray);">\n                    <li><strong>HTTPS:</strong> Encrypts web traffic (look for the padlock!)</li>\n                    <li><strong>End-to-end encryption:</strong> Messaging apps like Signal, WhatsApp</li>\n                    <li><strong>Full disk encryption:</strong> Protects data if device is stolen</li>\n                </ul>\n            </section>\n\n            <!-- Section 5 -->\n            <section class="lesson-section">\n                <h2>Safe Browsing Practices</h2>\n                \n                <h3>Recognizing Secure Websites</h3>\n                <ul style="margin-left: 1.5rem; color: var(--text-gray);">\n                    <li>Look for "https://" (not just "http://")</li>\n                    <li>Check for the padlock icon in the address bar</li>\n                    <li>Verify the domain name is correct (no typos!)</li>\n                    <li>Be wary of shortened URLs (bit.ly, etc.)</li>\n                </ul>\n                \n                <h3>Download Safety</h3>\n                <ul style="margin-left: 1.5rem; color: var(--text-gray);">\n                    <li>Only download from official sources</li>\n                    <li>Be cautious of "free" software - it may include malware</li>\n                    <li>Scan downloaded files with antivirus software</li>\n                    <li>Don\'t open unexpected email attachments</li>\n                </ul>\n                \n                <h3>Public WiFi Risks</h3>\n                <p>Public WiFi networks (coffee shops, airports) are often unsecured. Others on the network could potentially see your traffic.</p>\n                \n                <div class="tip-box">\n                    <svg viewBox="0 0 24 24" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg">\n                        <path d="M12 2C6.48 2 2 6.48 2 12s4.48 10 10 10 10-4.48 10-10S17.52 2 12 2zm1 15h-2v-6h2v6zm0-8h-2V7h2v2z"/>\n                    </svg>\n                    <p><strong>Public WiFi Safety:</strong> Use a VPN (Virtual Private Network) on public WiFi. It creates an encrypted tunnel for your traffic, keeping it private from others on the network.</p>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n\n            <!-- Section 6 -->\n            <section class="lesson-section">\n                <h2>Keeping Software Updated</h2>\n                <p>Software updates often include security patches for newly discovered vulnerabilities.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code><span class="comment">// Why updates matter:</span>\n\n<span class="number">1.</span> <span class="variable">Vulnerability discovered</span> → Hackers start exploiting it\n<span class="number">2.</span> <span class="function">Developer creates patch</span>   → Fixes the security hole\n<span class="number">3.</span> <span class="function">Update released</span>          → Available to users\n<span class="number">4.</span> <span class="keyword">You install update</span>       → Now protected!\n\n<span class="comment">// If you don\'t update, you remain vulnerable!</span></code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <h3>What to Update</h3>\n                <ul style="margin-left: 1.5rem; color: var(--text-gray);">\n                    <li><strong>Operating System:</strong> Enable automatic updates</li>\n                    <li><strong>Browsers:</strong> Usually auto-update, but check</li>\n                    <li><strong>Applications:</strong> Especially security software</li>\n                    <li><strong>Antivirus:</strong> Must update for new threat definitions</li>\n                </ul>\n            </section>\n\n            <!-- Section 7 -->\n            <section class="lesson-section">\n                <h2>Backup and Recovery</h2>\n                <p>Security isn\'t just about prevention - it\'s also about being able to recover if something goes wrong.</p>\n                \n                <h3>The 3-2-1 Backup Rule</h3>\n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code><span class="comment">// 3-2-1 Backup Strategy:</span>\n\n<span class="number">3</span> copies of your data\n<span class="number">2</span> different storage types\n<span class="number">1</span> copy offsite (cloud or different location)\n\n<span class="comment">// Example:</span>\n- <span class="variable">Original</span> on your computer\n- <span class="variable">Backup</span> on external hard drive\n- <span class="variable">Backup</span> in cloud storage (Google Drive, Dropbox)</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <p>This ensures that even if your computer is lost, stolen, or hit by ransomware, you can recover your data.</p>\n            </section>\n\n            <!-- Key Takeaways -->\n            <section class="lesson-section">\n                <h2>Key Takeaways</h2>\n                <div class="tip-box">\n 15h-2v-6h2v6zm0-8h-2V7h2v2z"/>\n                    </svg>\n                    <div>\n                        <p><strong>Remember:</strong></p>\n                        <ul style="margin-top: 0.5rem; margin-left: 1.5rem;">\n                            <li><strong>Threats:</strong> Malware, phishing, social engineering</li>\n                            <li><strong>Passwords:</strong> Use strong, unique passwords and a password manager</li>\n                            <li><strong>2FA:</strong> Enable two-factor authentication everywhere possible</li>\n                            <li><strong>Encryption:</strong> Protects data in transit and at rest</li>\n                            <li><strong>Updates:</strong> Keep all software updated for security patches</li>\n                            <li><strong>Backups:</strong> Follow the 3-2-1 rule for data protection</li>\n                        </ul>\n                    </div>\n                </div>\n                \n It\'s the standard language used to create and structure content on the web. Every website you visit is built with HTML at its core.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-explanation">\n                    <p><strong>Breaking down the name:</strong><br>\n                    <strong>HyperText:</strong> Text that links to other text (like clicking links)<br>\n                    <strong>Markup:</strong> Tags that define how content is structured<br>\n                    <strong>Language:</strong> A standardized way to communicate instructions</p>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n\n            <!-- Section 2 -->\n            <section class="lesson-section">\n                <h2>HTML is Not a Programming Language</h2>\n                <p>HTML is a <strong>markup language</strong>, not a programming language. It doesn\'t have logic, variables, or calculations. It simply describes the structure and content of a webpage.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code><span class="comment">// Programming languages (like JavaScript) can:</span>\n<span class="keyword">if</span> (temperature > <span class="number">30</span>) {\n    <span class="function">showMessage</span>(<span class="string">"It\'s hot!"</span>);\n}\n\n<span class="comment">// HTML only describes structure:</span>\n&lt;<span class="keyword">p</span>&gt;The temperature is 30 degrees.&lt;/<span class="keyword">p</span>&gt;</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <div class="tip-box">\n                    <svg viewBox="0 0 24 24" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg">\n                        <path d="M12 2C6.48 2 2 6.48 2 12s4.48 10 10 10 10-4.48 10-10S17.52 2 12 2zm1 15h-2v-6h2v6zm0-8h-2V7h2v2z"/>\n                    </svg>\n                    <p><strong>Think of HTML as:</strong> The skeleton of a website. CSS adds the skin and clothes (style), and JavaScript adds the muscles and movement (behavior).</p>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n\n            <!-- Section 3 -->\n            <section class="lesson-section">\n                <h2>HTML Tags and Elements</h2>\n                <p>HTML uses <strong>tags</strong> to mark up content. Tags tell the browser what each piece of content is.</p>\n                \n                <h3>Tag Syntax</h3>\n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code><span class="comment">// Basic tag structure:</span>\n&lt;<span class="keyword">tagname</span>&gt;Content goes here&lt;/<span class="keyword">tagname</span>&gt;\n ↑          ↑                    ↑\nOpening    Content              Closing\ntag                             tag\n\n<span class="comment">// Example:</span>\n&lt;<span class="keyword">p</span>&gt;This is a paragraph.&lt;/<span class="keyword">p</span>&gt;\n\n<span class="comment">// The opening and closing tags wrap the content.</span>\n<span class="comment">// The closing tag always has a forward slash (/).</span></code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <h3>Self-Closing Tags</h3>\n                <p>Some tags don\'t have content and close themselves:</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code><span class="comment">// Self-closing tags (void elements):</span>\n&lt;<span class="keyword">img</span> <span class="variable">src</span>=<span class="string">"photo.jpg"</span> /&gt;    <span class="comment">// Image</span>\n&lt;<span class="keyword">br</span> /&gt;                   <span class="comment">// Line break</span>\n&lt;<span class="keyword">hr</span> /&gt;                   <span class="comment">// Horizontal rule</span>\n&lt;<span class="keyword">input</span> <span class="variable">type</span>=<span class="string">"text"</span> /&gt;    <span class="comment">// Input field</span>\n\n<span class="comment">// In HTML5, the slash is optional:</span>\n&lt;<span class="keyword">img</span> <span class="variable">src</span>=<span class="string">"photo.jpg"</span>&gt;     <span class="comment">// Also valid</span>\n&lt;<span class="keyword">br</span>&gt;                    <span class="comment">// Also valid</span></code></pre>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n\n            <!-- Section 4 -->\n            <section class="lesson-section">\n                <h2>HTML Elements</h2>\n                <p>An <strong>element</strong> includes the opening tag, content, and closing tag (or just the tag for self-closing elements).</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code><span class="comment">// An element is the complete package:</span>\n┌─────────────────────────────────────┐\n│ &lt;<span class="keyword">h1</span>&gt;Welcome to My Website&lt;/<span class="keyword">h1</span>&gt;    │\n│ ↑↑↑↑↑↑↑↑↑↑↑↑↑↑↑↑↑↑↑↑↑↑↑↑↑↑↑↑↑↑↑↑↑↑ │\n│       This entire line = Element     │\n└─────────────────────────────────────┘\n\n<span class="comment">// Common elements you\'ll use:</span>\n&lt;<span class="keyword">h1</span>&gt;Heading 1&lt;/<span class="keyword">h1</span>&gt;           <span class="comment">// Main heading</span>\n&lt;<span class="keyword">p</span>&gt;Paragraph text&lt;/<span class="keyword">p</span>&gt;       <span class="comment">// Paragraph</span>\n&lt;<span class="keyword">a</span>&gt;Click here&lt;/<span class="keyword">a</span>&gt;           <span class="comment">// Link</span>\n&lt;<span class="keyword">div</span>&gt;Content&lt;/<span class="keyword">div</span>&gt;         <span class="comment">// Container</span>\n&lt;<span class="keyword">span</span>&gt;Inline text&lt;/<span class="keyword">span</span>&gt;     <span class="comment">// Inline container</span></code></pre>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n\n            <!-- Section 5 -->\n            <section class="lesson-section">\n                <h2>Nesting Elements</h2>\n                <p>Elements can be placed inside other elements. This is called <strong>nesting</strong>.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code><span class="comment">// Nested elements:</span>\n&lt;<span class="keyword">div</span>&gt;\n    &lt;<span class="keyword">h1</span>&gt;My Title&lt;/<span class="keyword">h1</span>&gt;\n    &lt;<span class="keyword">p</span>&gt;This is a &lt;<span class="keyword">strong</span>&gt;bold&lt;/<span class="keyword">strong</span>&gt; word.&lt;/<span class="keyword">p</span>&gt;\n&lt;/<span class="keyword">div</span>&gt;\n\n<span class="comment">// Correct nesting (tags close in reverse order):</span>\n&lt;<span class="keyword">div</span>&gt;&lt;<span class="keyword">p</span>&gt;Text&lt;/<span class="keyword">p</span>&gt;&lt;/<span class="keyword">div</span>&gt;  ✓ <span class="comment">// Correct</span>\n\n<span class="comment">// Wrong nesting (tags don\'t match):</span>\n&lt;<span class="keyword">div</span>&gt;&lt;<span class="keyword">p</span>&gt;Text&lt;/<span class="keyword">div</span>&gt;&lt;/<span class="keyword">p</span>&gt;  ✗ <span class="comment">// Wrong!</span></code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <div class="tip-box">\n                    <svg viewBox="0 0 24 24" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg">\n                        <path d="M12 2C6.48 2 2 6.48 2 12s4.48 10 10 10 10-4.48 10-10S17.52 2 12 2zm1 15h-2v-6h2v6zm0-8h-2V7h2v2z"/>\n                    </svg>\n                    <p><strong>Rule:</strong> Always close tags in the reverse order you opened them. Think of it like opening and closing parentheses in math.</p>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n\n            <!-- Section 6 -->\n            <section class="lesson-section">\n                <h2>HTML Attributes</h2>\n                <p>Attributes provide extra information about elements. They go in the opening tag.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code><span class="comment">// Attribute syntax:</span>\n&lt;<span class="keyword">tag</span> <span class="variable">attribute</span>=<span class="string">"value"</span>&gt;Content&lt;/<span class="keyword">tag</span>&gt;\n\n<span class="comment">// Real examples:</span>\n&lt;<span class="keyword">a</span> <span class="variable">href</span>=<span class="string">"https://google.com"</span>&gt;Go to Google&lt;/<span class="keyword">a</span>&gt;\n&lt;<span class="keyword">img</span> <span class="variable">src</span>=<span class="string">"photo.jpg"</span> <span class="variable">alt</span>=<span class="string">"A beautiful sunset"</span>&gt;\n&lt;<span class="keyword">p</span> <span class="variable">class</span>=<span class="string">"intro"</span>&gt;Welcome!&lt;/<span class="keyword">p</span>&gt;\n&lt;<span class="keyword">input</span> <span class="variable">type</span>=<span class="string">"text"</span> <span class="variable">placeholder</span>=<span class="string">"Enter name"</span>&gt;</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <h3>Common Attributes</h3>\n                <ul style="margin-left: 1.5rem; color: var(--text-gray);">\n                    <li><strong>id:</strong> Unique identifier for an element</li>\n                    <li><strong>class:</strong> Groups elements for styling</li>\n                    <li><strong>src:</strong> Source URL for images/media</li>\n                    <li><strong>href:</strong> URL for links</li>\n                    <li><strong>alt:</strong> Alternative text for images</li>\n                    <li><strong>style:</strong> Inline CSS styles</li>\n                </ul>\n            </section>\n\n            <!-- Section 7 -->\n            <section class="lesson-section">\n                <h2>How HTML is Rendered</h2>\n                <p>When you visit a website, here\'s what happens:</p>\n                \n                <ol style="margin-left: 1.5rem; color: var(--text-gray);">\n                    <li>The browser requests an HTML file from a server</li>\n                    <li>The server sends the HTML code</li>\n                    <li>The browser parses (reads) the HTML</li>\n                    <li>It builds a DOM (Document Object Model) tree</li>\n                    <li>It renders the visible page from the DOM</li>\n                </ol>\n                \n                <div class="code-explanation">\n                    <p><strong>DOM:</strong> The Document Object Model is how the browser represents HTML as a tree structure. Each element is a "node" that JavaScript can interact with.</p>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n\n            <!-- Key Takeaways -->\n            <section class="lesson-section">\n                <h2>Key Takeaways</h2>\n                <div class="tip-box">\n                    <svg viewBox="0 0 24 24" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg">\n                        <path d="M12 2C6.48 2 2 6.48 2 12s4.48 10 10 10 10-4.48 10-10S17.52 2 12 2zm1 15h-2v-6h2v6zm0-8h-2V7h2v2z"/>\n                    </svg>\n                    <div>\n                        <p><strong>Remember:</strong></p>\n                        <ul style="margin-top: 0.5rem; margin-left: 1.5rem;">\n                            <li><strong>HTML:</strong> A markup language for structuring web content</li>\n                            <li><strong>Tags:</strong> Labels that define elements (like &lt;p&gt;, &lt;h1&gt;)</li>\n                            <li><strong>Elements:</strong> Opening tag + content + closing tag</li>\n                            <li><strong>Attributes:</strong> Extra info added to opening tags</li>\n                            <li><strong>Nesting:</strong> Putting elements inside other elements</li>\n                            <li><strong>Closing order:</strong> Close tags in reverse order of opening</li>\n                        </ul>\n                    </div>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n\n            <!-- Navigation -->\n            <div class="nav-buttons">\n                <a href="index.html" class="nav-btn prev">← Back to Course</a>\n                <a href="lesson2.html" class="nav-btn next">Next: Document Structure →</a>\n            </div>\n        </div>\n    </main>\n\n    <!-- Footer -->\n    <footer class="footer">\n        <p>© 2024 Learner. This is the foundation of every webpage you\'ll create.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code><span class="keyword">&lt;!DOCTYPE html&gt;</span>\n&lt;<span class="keyword">html</span> <span class="variable">lang</span>=<span class="string">"en"</span>&gt;\n&lt;<span class="keyword">head</span>&gt;\n    &lt;<span class="keyword">meta</span> <span class="variable">charset</span>=<span class="string">"UTF-8"</span>&gt;\n    &lt;<span class="keyword">meta</span> <span class="variable">name</span>=<span class="string">"viewport"</span> <span class="variable">content</span>=<span class="string">"width=device-width, initial-scale=1.0"</span>&gt;\n    &lt;<span class="keyword">title</span>&gt;My First Webpage&lt;/<span class="keyword">title</span>&gt;\n&lt;/<span class="keyword">head</span>&gt;\n&lt;<span class="keyword">body</span>&gt;\n    &lt;<span class="keyword">h1</span>&gt;Hello, World!&lt;/<span class="keyword">h1</span>&gt;\n    &lt;<span class="keyword">p</span>&gt;This is my first webpage.&lt;/<span class="keyword">p</span>&gt;\n&lt;/<span class="keyword">body</span>&gt;\n&lt;/<span class="keyword">html</span>&gt;</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <p>Let\'s break down each part to understand what it does.</p>\n            </section>\n\n            <!-- Section 2 -->\n            <section class="lesson-section">\n                <h2>The DOCTYPE Declaration</h2>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code><span class="keyword">&lt;!DOCTYPE html&gt;</span></code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <p>This tells the browser that this is an HTML5 document. It must be the very first line in your HTML file, before any other code. Without it, browsers may display your page in "quirks mode" (older, inconsistent rendering).</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-explanation">\n                    <p><strong>Why it matters:</strong> In the past, there were different versions of HTML with different DOCTYPEs. The simple HTML5 DOCTYPE tells modern browsers to use the latest standards.</p>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n\n            <!-- Section 3 -->\n            <section class="lesson-section">\n                <h2>The html Element</h2>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>&lt;<span class="keyword">html</span> <span class="variable">lang</span>=<span class="string">"en"</span>&gt;\n    <span class="comment">// All page content goes here</span>\n&lt;/<span class="keyword">html</span>&gt;</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <p>The <code>&lt;html&gt;</code> element is the root element that contains all other elements. Everything on your page goes inside it.</p>\n                \n                <h3>The lang Attribute</h3>\n                <p>The <code>lang</code> attribute specifies the language of the content:</p>\n                <ul style="margin-left: 1.5rem; color: var(--text-gray);">\n                    <li><code>lang="en"</code> - English</li>\n                    <li><code>lang="es"</code> - Spanish</li>\n                    <li><code>lang="fr"</code> - French</li>\n                    <li><code>lang="zh"</code> - Chinese</li>\n                </ul>\n                \n                <div class="tip-box">\n                    <svg viewBox="0 0 24 24" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg">\n                        <path d="M12 2C6.48 2 2 6.48 2 12s4.48 10 10 10 10-4.48 10-10S17.52 2 12 2zm1 15h-2v-6h2v6zm0-8h-2V7h2v2z"/>\n                    </svg>\n                    <p><strong>Why lang matters:</strong> It helps screen readers pronounce content correctly and enables proper spell-checking in browsers.</p>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n\n            <!-- Section 4 -->\n            <section class="lesson-section">\n                <h2>The head Element</h2>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>&lt;<span class="keyword">head</span>&gt;\n    <span class="comment">// Metadata goes here (not visible on page)</span>\n    &lt;<span class="keyword">meta</span> <span class="variable">charset</span>=<span class="string">"UTF-8"</span>&gt;\n    &lt;<span class="keyword">meta</span> <span class="variable">name</span>=<span class="string">"viewport"</span> <span class="variable">content</span>=<span class="string">"width=device-width, initial-scale=1.0"</span>&gt;\n    &lt;<span class="keyword">title</span>&gt;Page Title&lt;/<span class="keyword">title</span>&gt;\n    &lt;<span class="keyword">link</span> <span class="variable">rel</span>=<span class="string">"stylesheet"</span> <span class="variable">href</span>=<span class="string">"styles.css"</span>&gt;\n&lt;/<span class="keyword">head</span>&gt;</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <p>The <code>&lt;head&gt;</code> contains <strong>metadata</strong> - information about the page that isn\'t displayed. This includes:</p>\n                \n                <h3>Meta Tags</h3>\n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code><span class="comment">// Character encoding (required for special characters):</span>\n&lt;<span class="keyword">meta</span> <span class="variable">charset</span>=<span class="string">"UTF-8"</span>&gt;\n\n<span class="comment">// Viewport for responsive design:</span>\n&lt;<span class="keyword">meta</span> <span class="variable">name</span>=<span class="string">"viewport"</span> <span class="variable">content</span>=<span class="string">"width=device-width, initial-scale=1.0"</span>&gt;\n\n<span class="comment">// Description for search engines:</span>\n&lt;<span class="keyword">meta</span> <span class="variable">name</span>=<span class="string">"description"</span> <span class="variable">content</span>=<span class="string">"A description of your page"</span>&gt;\n\n<span class="comment">// Author information:</span>\n&lt;<span class="keyword">meta</span> <span class="variable">name</span>=<span class="string">"author"</span> <span class="variable">content</span>=<span class="string">"Your Name"</span>&gt;</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <h3>The title Element</h3>\n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>&lt;<span class="keyword">title</span>&gt;My Awesome Website&lt;/<span class="keyword">title</span>&gt;</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                <p>The title appears in the browser tab and is used by search engines. Make it descriptive!</p>\n                \n                <h3>Linking External Resources</h3>\n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code><span class="comment">// Link to CSS stylesheet:</span>\n&lt;<span class="keyword">link</span> <span class="variable">rel</span>=<span class="string">"stylesheet"</span> <span class="variable">href</span>=<span class="string">"styles.css"</span>&gt;\n\n<span class="comment">// Link to favicon (tab icon):</span>\n&lt;<span class="keyword">link</span> <span class="variable">rel</span>=<span class="string">"icon"</span> <span class="variable">href</span>=<span class="string">"favicon.ico"</span>&gt;</code></pre>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n\n            <!-- Section 5 -->\n            <section class="lesson-section">\n                <h2>The body Element</h2>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code>&lt;<span class="keyword">body</span>&gt;\n    <span class="comment">// All visible content goes here</span>\n    &lt;<span class="keyword">h1</span>&gt;Welcome to My Website&lt;/<span class="keyword">h1</span>&gt;\n    &lt;<span class="keyword">p</span>&gt;This is visible content.&lt;/<span class="keyword">p</span>&gt;\n    &lt;<span class="keyword">img</span> <span class="variable">src</span>=<span class="string">"photo.jpg"</span> <span class="variable">alt</span>=<span class="string">"A photo"</span>&gt;\n&lt;/<span class="keyword">body</span>&gt;</code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <p>The <code>&lt;body&gt;</code> contains everything visible on the page: text, images, videos, forms, and more. Everything you want users to see goes here.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-explanation">\n                    <p><strong>head vs body:</strong> The head is for metadata (information about the page). The body is for content (what users actually see).</p>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n\n            <!-- Section 6 -->\n            <section class="lesson-section">\n                <h2>HTML Comments</h2>\n                <p>Comments are notes in your code that aren\'t displayed. They help document your code.</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code><span class="comment">&lt;!-- This is a comment. It won\'t appear on the page. --&gt;</span>\n\n&lt;<span class="keyword">p</span>&gt;This text is visible.&lt;/<span class="keyword">p</span>&gt; <span class="comment">&lt;!-- Inline comment --&gt;</span>\n\n<span class="comment">&lt;!-- \n    Multi-line comments \n    can span multiple lines.\n    Useful for longer notes or temporarily hiding code.\n--&gt;</span></code></pre>\n                </div>\n                \n                <div class="tip-box">\n                    <svg viewBox="0 0 24 24" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg">\n                        <path d="M12 2C6.48 2 2 6.48 2 12s4.48 10 10 10 10-4.48 10-10S17.52 2 12 2zm1 15h-2v-6h2v6zm0-8h-2V7h2v2z"/>\n                    </svg>\n                    <p><strong>Use comments to:</strong> Explain complex code, leave notes for yourself or others, temporarily disable code during debugging, and document your thought process.</p>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n\n            <!-- Section 7 -->\n            <section class="lesson-section">\n                <h2>Complete Example</h2>\n                <p>Here\'s a complete, properly structured HTML document:</p>\n                \n                <div class="code-block">\n                    <pre><code><span class="keyword">&lt;!DOCTYPE html&gt;</span>\n&lt;<span class="keyword">html</span> <span class="variable">lang</span>=<span class="string">"en"</span>&gt;\n&lt;<span class="keyword">head</span>&gt;\n    &lt;<span class="keyword">meta</span> <span class="variable">charset</span>=<span class="string">"UTF-8"</span>&gt;\n    &lt;<span class="keyword">meta</span> <span class="variable">name</span>=<span class="string">"viewport"</span> <span class="variable">content</span>=<span class="string">"width=device-width, initial-scale=1.0"</span>&gt;\n    &lt;<span class="keyword">meta</span> <span class="variable">name</span>=<span class="string">"description"</span> <span class="variable">content</span>=<span class="string">"A simple webpage"</span>&gt;\n    &lt;<span class="keyword">title</span>&gt;My First Webpage&lt;/<span class="keyword">title</span>&gt;\n&lt;/<span class="keyword">head</span>&gt;\n&lt;<span class="keyword">body</span>&gt;\n    <span class="comment">&lt;!-- Main heading --&gt;</span>\n    &lt;<span class="keyword">h1</span>&gt;Welcome!&lt;/<span class="keyword">h1</span>&gt;\n    \n    <span class="comment">&lt;!-- Introduction paragraph --&gt;</span>\n    &lt;<span class="keyword">p</span>&gt;This is my first webpage. I\'m learning HTML!&lt;/<span class="keyword">p</span>&gt;\n    \n    <span class="comment">&lt;!-- A link --&gt;</span>\n    &lt;<span class="keyword">a</span> <span class="variable">href</span>=<span class="string">"https://example.com"</span>&gt;Click here&lt;/<span class="keyword">a</span>&gt;\n&lt;/<span class="keyword">body</span>&gt;\n&lt;/<span class="keyword">html</span>&gt;</code></pre>\n                </div>\n            </section>\n\n            <!-- Key Takeaways -->\n            <section class="lesson-section">\n                <h2>Key Takeaways</h2>\n                <div class="tip-box">\n                    <svg viewBox="0 0 24 24" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg">\n                        <path d="M12 2C6.48 2 2 6.48 2 12s4.48 10 10 10 10-4.48 10-10S17.52 2 12 2zm1 15h-2v-6h2v6zm0-8h-2V7h2v2z"/>\n                    </svg>\n                    <div>\n                        <p><strong>Remember:</strong></p>\n                        <ul style="margin-top: 0.5rem;
